URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS491516279	2017-04-28 16:48:06	3400	species	Lesser Nighthawk	Chordeiles acutipennis			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Nye	US-NV-023	US-NV_977	33	USFWS_350		MQC-50885	L5595870	P	36.4019001	-116.2931377	2007-05-19		obsr857006	S36355365	Incidental	P20	EBIRD				1	0		0	1	0				
URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS221982550	2016-01-05 16:03:18	3400	species	Lesser Nighthawk	Chordeiles acutipennis			X				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Nye	US-NV-023		33			Beatty	L862152	H	36.9083648	-116.7592621	2007-05-10	15:00:00	obsr439228	S16024915	Historical	P62	EBIRD				1	0		0	1	0		Regrouping, I picked out a local motel (Phoenix Inn on the sign, but now called the Amargosa River Motel) and again inquired about the toad. The clerk informed me that the toads were commonly seen after dark, and suggested that I try the creek again. The temperature was in the 90's, but it was a dry heat that made it bearable.----As dusk fell, I headed creek-side and saw quite a few birds in the willows. DUSKY FLYCATCHER, BULLOCK'S ORIOLE, WHITE-CROWNED SPARROW, LINCOLN'S SPARROW, WILSON'S WARBLER, YELLOW WARBLER, C. YELLOWTHROAT, NO. MOCKINGBIRD, BLACK PHOEBE, WHITE-FACED IBIS, SNOWY EGRET, LESSER NIGHTHAWK, BROWN-HEADED COWBIRD, andGREAT-TAILED GRACKLE were all present. In addition, seven WILD BURROs crossed the creek and the parking lot.----Pools full of tadpoles were all along the riparian corridor. Finally, I found an adult AMARGOSA TOAD. As I gently held the toad, it felt cool and moist. After a nice little tete a tete, I set the toad back into the streamside sedges and wished it a long and happy life.----Being close to Death Valley, I thought that a little night drive might be in order. Although conditions were excellent, I didn't see a lot moving around. At least, I did see a couple of DESERT BANDED GECKOs, DARK KANGAROO MOUSE, MERRIAM'S K-RAT, PANAMINT K-RAT, and a MOJAVE SIDEWINDER.----The Sidewinder is kind of an old friend of mine. They are a highly evolved species, and like this young "winder" it remained perfectly still as it thermoregulated on the warm pavement. With it's little horns over the eyes, small size, and striped face, it was almost tempting to pick it up. However, I know that a sidewinder is quite venomous, and it must be respected regardless of size.--After I left the sidewinder unmolested, I once more looked up into black starry velvet of the desert night sky. With virtually no artificial light interference, the clear night sky is always marvel to behold.----I loved this birdy, toad friendly, unpretentious town! I saw the endemic AMARGOSA TOAD in the creek behind my motel!
